[[Source]](https://starwars.fandom.com/wiki/Template:Religion)

:   "*Being a Jedi is not just about* power*, or lightsabers, or even skill with the Force. It is about* connection*. Being part of something bigger. I am stronger as part of the Jedi Order than I could ever be alone.*"
:   ―Obi-Wan Kenobi, to Anakin Skywalker[[42]](#cite_note-Obi-Wan_and_Anakin_5-42)

The **Jedi Order**, also known as the **Order of the Jedi**, and the **New Jedi Order** under [Jedi Master](/wiki/Jedi_Master "Jedi Master") [Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Luke_Skywalker "Luke Skywalker"), was a noble monastic and nontheistic [religious](/wiki/Religion "Religion") order united in their devotion to the [light side of the Force](/wiki/Light_side_of_the_Force "Light side of the Force"). They served as mediators, warriors, and with teaching and exploratory efforts. With a [history](/wiki/Timeline_of_galactic_history "Timeline of galactic history") dating back [thousands of years](/wiki/Millennium "Millennium") before the [rise](/wiki/Imperial_Era "Imperial Era") of the [Galactic Empire](/wiki/Galactic_Empire "Galactic Empire"), the [Jedi Knights](/wiki/Jedi_Knight "Jedi Knight")—noted for their [lightsabers](/wiki/Lightsaber "Lightsaber") and [natural](/wiki/Midi-chlorian "Midi-chlorian") [ability](/wiki/Force-sensitive "Force-sensitive") to harness the [powers](/wiki/Force_power "Force power") of [the Force](/wiki/The_Force "The Force")—stood as the [guardians of peace and justice](/wiki/Law_enforcement_agency "Law enforcement agency") in the [Galactic Republic](/wiki/Galactic_Republic "Galactic Republic"). The Order was originally established on [Ahch-To](/wiki/Ahch-To "Ahch-To") in the [Unknown Regions](/wiki/Unknown_Regions "Unknown Regions"). In later years, the [Jedi Grand Temple](/wiki/Imperial_Palace "Imperial Palace") on the [Core World](/wiki/Core_Worlds "Core Worlds") [Coruscant](/wiki/Coruscant "Coruscant") served as the hub of all [Jedi](/wiki/Jedi "Jedi") activity in [the galaxy](/wiki/The_galaxy "The galaxy"). The [Temple](/wiki/Jedi_temple "Jedi temple") was also a [training](/wiki/Jedi_training "Jedi training") school for [younglings](/wiki/Jedi_Initiate "Jedi Initiate") and [Padawans](/wiki/Padawan "Padawan"), who learned the ways of the Force under the supervision of Jedi Masters, twelve of whom were elected to serve on the [Jedi High Council](/wiki/Jedi_High_Council "Jedi High Council")—the Order's highest governing authority. The High [Council's](/wiki/Jedi_Council "Jedi Council") staff [officers](/wiki/Officer "Officer") were the [Grand Master](/wiki/Grand_Master "Grand Master"), who functioned as the leader of the Order and was a title reserved for the wisest Jedi Master, and the [Master of the Order](/wiki/Master_of_the_Order "Master of the Order"), who served as the Council's appointed leader. The [Jedi Code](/wiki/Jedi_Code "Jedi Code") governed the Order's way of life; therefore, every Jedi was duty-bound to observe and uphold the Code or else risk expulsion from the Order.

The emergence of the [Sith](/wiki/Sith "Sith") Order was the result of a [schism](/wiki/Hundred-Year_Darkness "Hundred-Year Darkness") that fractured Jedi unity, dividing the Order between the Jedi who remained faithful to the light and a [group of renegades](/wiki/Jedi_splinter_group "Jedi splinter group") that followed a [rogue Jedi](/wiki/Unidentified_rogue_Jedi "Unidentified rogue Jedi") into exile for exploring the [dark side of the Force](/wiki/Dark_side_of_the_Force "Dark side of the Force"). Thenceforth, the Jedi and Sith [warred](/wiki/Sith_war_(Old_Republic) "Sith war (Old Republic)") with each other for [centuries](/wiki/Standard_century "Standard century"). Although the [last conflict](/wiki/Jedi-Sith_War "Jedi-Sith War") concluded with the [fall of the Old Republic](/wiki/Fall_of_the_Old_Republic "Fall of the Old Republic"), the ancient Sith all but perished as well, allowing a new [Galactic](/wiki/Galaxy "Galaxy") Republic to rise under the protection of the Jedi Order. Unknown to the Jedi, however, the Sith endured in secret for a millennium beginning with [Darth Bane](/wiki/Darth_Bane "Darth Bane"), the sole-surviving [Dark Lord of the Sith](/wiki/Dark_Lord_of_the_Sith "Dark Lord of the Sith") who reformed the [Sith way](/wiki/Code_of_the_Sith "Code of the Sith") by creating the [Rule of Two](/wiki/Rule_of_Two "Rule of Two")—a rule limiting the Sith Order's ranks to two members: a [Sith Master](/wiki/Sith_Master "Sith Master") to embody the power of the dark side, and a [Sith apprentice](/wiki/Sith_apprentice "Sith apprentice") to covet that power. While the Jedi and Republic moved on, their ancient wars with the Sith fading from memory, Bane's legacy spawned a lineage of [Sith Lords](/wiki/Sith_Lord "Sith Lord") that culminated in the rise of [Darth Sidious](/wiki/Darth_Sidious "Darth Sidious") approximately [three decades](/wiki/32_BBY "32 BBY") before the [Battle of Yavin](/wiki/Battle_of_Yavin "Battle of Yavin").

During the [final decades](/wiki/Republic_Era "Republic Era") of the Republic, the Jedi Order vowed allegiance to the [Galactic Senate](/wiki/Galactic_Senate "Galactic Senate") as the galaxy was beset by [political](/wiki/Politics "Politics") instability and social unrest which, in turn, created a [secessionist crisis](/wiki/Separatist_Crisis "Separatist Crisis") that ultimately resulted in the formation of the [Confederacy of Independent Systems](/wiki/Confederacy_of_Independent_Systems "Confederacy of Independent Systems"). Lacking the sufficient manpower needed to protect the galaxy, the Jedi became [commanders](/wiki/Jedi_Commander "Jedi Commander") and [generals](/wiki/Jedi_General "Jedi General") in the newly-formed [Grand Army of the Republic](/wiki/Grand_Army_of_the_Republic "Grand Army of the Republic"). For roughly three years they commanded [armies](/wiki/Army "Army") of [clone troopers](/wiki/Clone_trooper "Clone trooper") in a conflict known as the [Clone Wars](/wiki/Clone_Wars "Clone Wars"), engaging the Confederacy's [battle droid](/wiki/Battle_droid "Battle droid") [forces](/wiki/Confederacy_military "Confederacy military") led by [Count](/wiki/Count "Count") [Dooku](/wiki/Dooku "Dooku")—a former Jedi Master who became a Sith [Lord](/wiki/Lord "Lord")—and the [cybernetic](/wiki/Cyborg "Cyborg") [warlord](/wiki/Warlord "Warlord") [General](/wiki/General "General") [Grievous](/wiki/Grievous "Grievous"). Though the Jedi fought to preserve the Republic, the government they served was secretly taken over by Sidious who, as [Senator](/wiki/Senator "Senator") Sheev Palpatine of [Naboo](/wiki/Naboo "Naboo"), rose to power in the Senate and became the last [Supreme Chancellor](/wiki/Supreme_Chancellor "Supreme Chancellor") of the Republic. The Jedi were unknowingly being deceived by the Sith.

The Chancellor's deceptions and machinations culminated in the execution of [Order 66](/wiki/Order_66 "Order 66"), a [secret protocol](/wiki/Executive_Order_Codes_for_the_Grand_Army_of_the_Republic "Executive Order Codes for the Grand Army of the Republic") that [forcibly turned](/wiki/Behavioral_modification_biochip "Behavioral modification biochip") the Jedi's [clone](/wiki/Cloning "Cloning") [soldiers](/wiki/Soldier "Soldier") against them, leading to an all but total [extermination](/wiki/Great_Jedi_Purge "Great Jedi Purge") of the Jedi Order. With most of the Jedi eliminated, Sidious [supplanted](/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_New_Order "Proclamation of the New Order") a thousand years of [democracy](/wiki/Democracy "Democracy") with a [new government](/wiki/New_Order "New Order") known as the Galactic Empire. In addition, Sidious succeeded in turning [Anakin Skywalker](/wiki/Anakin_Skywalker "Anakin Skywalker")—the prophesied [Chosen One](/wiki/Chosen_One "Chosen One") who was destined to bring balance to the Force by destroying the Sith—to the dark side and renamed him Darth Vader. As a Sith Lord, the former Jedi Knight served the self-proclaimed [Galactic Emperor](/wiki/Galactic_Emperor "Galactic Emperor") by hunting down the few surviving Jedi, who had gone into hiding across the galaxy. In spite of the Sith's efforts, however, the Jedi continued to endure. Within a generation of the Empire's rise to power, [Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Obi-Wan Kenobi") and [Yoda](/wiki/Yoda "Yoda")—both of whom survived the initial purge of the Order—trained Vader's son, Luke Skywalker, in the Jedi arts. Luke would later redeem his father, causing the redeemed Anakin Skywalker to return to the light and fulfill his destiny as the Chosen One, [destroying](/wiki/Death "Death") both himself and his Master during the [Battle of Endor](/wiki/Battle_of_Endor "Battle of Endor").

The Empire [dissolved](/wiki/Galactic_Concordance "Galactic Concordance") into various remnants as a result of their [defeat](/wiki/Battle_of_Jakku "Battle of Jakku") in the [Galactic Civil War](/wiki/Galactic_Civil_War "Galactic Civil War"), allowing the [Alliance to Restore the Republic](/wiki/Alliance_to_Restore_the_Republic "Alliance to Restore the Republic") to rise as the [New Republic](/wiki/New_Republic "New Republic"). Under the [new era](/wiki/New_Republic_Era "New Republic Era"), Luke Skywalker endeavored to rebuild the Order by training a new generation of Jedi. Among Skywalker's students was his nephew, [Ben Solo](/wiki/Ben_Solo "Ben Solo"), the son of his [twin](/wiki/Twin "Twin") sister, [Princess](/wiki/Princess "Princess") [Leia Organa](/wiki/Leia_Skywalker_Organa_Solo "Leia Skywalker Organa Solo"), and the famed [smuggler](/wiki/Smuggler "Smuggler") [Han Solo](/wiki/Han_Solo "Han Solo"). Ben, however, was seduced by the dark side of the Force at the coaxing of [Snoke](/wiki/Snoke "Snoke"), an enigmatic figure who spearheaded the Imperial-inspired [First Order](/wiki/First_Order "First Order"). Luke confronted and frightened Ben, who fought back and fled. As a result, Ben adopted the name and persona of Kylo Ren, a First Order [warlord](/wiki/Warlord "Warlord") and [master](/wiki/Ren "Ren") of the [Knights of Ren](/wiki/Knights_of_Ren "Knights of Ren").

The new generation was betrayed and [destroyed](/wiki/Destruction_of_the_Jedi_Temple "Destruction of the Jedi Temple") by Ren, who left the [Jedi training temple](/wiki/Jedi_Temple_of_Luke_Skywalker "Jedi Temple of Luke Skywalker") [burning](/wiki/Fire "Fire") by the [time](/wiki/Time "Time") Skywalker recovered from the attack. Feeling responsible for Ben's fall and the massacre of his apprentices, he went into exile and disappeared from the galaxy, leaving only traces of his location on a [star](/wiki/Star "Star") [map](/wiki/Map_to_Skywalker "Map to Skywalker"). The First Order and the [Resistance](/wiki/Resistance "Resistance") both sought to acquire the map, but ultimately it was the latter that succeeded due to the actions of the [Jakku](/wiki/Jakku "Jakku") [scavenger](/wiki/Scavenger "Scavenger") [Rey](/wiki/Rey_Skywalker "Rey Skywalker"). She followed the map to the [planet](/wiki/Planet "Planet") [Ahch-To](/wiki/Ahch-To "Ahch-To"), where the last Jedi had taken [refuge](/wiki/Hermit "Hermit") in the [first Jedi Temple](/wiki/First_Jedi_Temple "First Jedi Temple").

Skywalker, stricken by grief and believing his return would only cause more problems, was reluctant to train Rey or another generation of Jedi. However, the last Jedi eventually returned to the fight, buying time for the Resistance to escape the [siege of Crait](/wiki/Battle_of_Crait "Battle of Crait") led by Kylo Ren, who became the new [Supreme Leader](/wiki/Supreme_Leader "Supreme Leader") after [killing his master](/wiki/Battle_of_Oetchi "Battle of Oetchi"), Snoke. Skywalker became [one with the Force](/wiki/Force_spirit "Force spirit") after exerting a great amount of energy to [project](/wiki/Force_projection "Force projection") himself across the galaxy to face his fallen nephew, but not before acknowledging that he would not be the last Jedi. His heroic tale spread across the galaxy, inspiring others and giving hope in a [time of rising darkness](/wiki/First_Order-Resistance_War "First Order-Resistance War").

Having returned from death, Darth Sidious urged Kylo Ren to end the Jedi Order by killing Rey, who was his [granddaughter](/wiki/Palpatine_family "Palpatine family"). After Ren renounced the dark side, Sidious [attempted to turn](/wiki/Battle_of_Exegol "Battle of Exegol") Rey until he discovered her [bond](/wiki/Force-bond "Force-bond") with Ben Solo. Realizing they were a [dyad in the Force](/wiki/Force_dyad "Force dyad"), Sidious nearly drained them of their life force to regain his full power. Though weakened by Sidious’ attack, Rey was strengthened by the spirits of past Jedi, allowing the apprentice to stand against the Dark Lord of the Sith. She destroyed her grandfather using his own [Force lightning](/wiki/Force_lightning "Force lightning") against him, preventing the rebirth of the Sith Order, but the effort left her dead. Solo [resurrected](/wiki/Force_healing "Force healing") her at the cost of his life, becoming one with the Force as the last Skywalker. The Skywalkers were gone, but their legacy endured through Rey, who took the Skywalker name to honor her mentors and restore the Jedi Order.

## Description[]

### Overview[]

:   "*The Order tends to be what it needs to be for any particular time. Sometimes, we're warriors, fighting the forces of evil. Sometimes, we govern. Sometimes, we do the opposite—drawing inward, studying the Force and its mysteries. Sometimes, we explore. Sometimes, we do all of those things. And sometimes… We are carved down to almost nothing. Those who are left must bear the responsibility of being one last bit of light in a galaxy filled with endless dark.*"
:   ―Elzar Mann, to Luke Skywalker[[43]](#cite_note-Star_Wars_(2020)_20-43)

 [![For a thousand generations, the Jedi Order protected the Galactic Republic as guardians of peace and justice.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/The_High_Republic_The_Fallen_Star_unlettered_cover.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20210917181006) [![For a thousand generations, the Jedi Order protected the Galactic Republic as guardians of peace and justice.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/The_High_Republic_The_Fallen_Star_unlettered_cover.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20210917181006)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/The_High_Republic_The_Fallen_Star_unlettered_cover.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20210917181006) 

For a thousand generations, the Jedi Order protected the Galactic Republic as guardians of peace and justice.

 

The [Jedi Knights](/wiki/Jedi_Knight "Jedi Knight")[[44]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-44) were a noble order of [Force-sensitive](/wiki/Force-sensitive "Force-sensitive") protectors—united by their ability to use [the Force](/wiki/The_Force "The Force")—who upheld peace and justice in the [Galactic Republic](/wiki/Galactic_Republic "Galactic Republic") for over a thousand generations,[[4]](#cite_note-DB:Order-4) carrying out what they sensed to be the will of the Force as its instruments.[[28]](#cite_note-Light_of_the_Jedi-28) As [keepers of the peace](/wiki/Law_enforcement_agency "Law enforcement agency"), the [Jedi](/wiki/Jedi "Jedi") Order[[2]](#cite_note-UltimateSW-2)—also referred to as the Order of the Jedi[[45]](#cite_note-Day-45)—undertook [diplomatic](/wiki/Politics "Politics") missions on behalf of the [Galactic Senate](/wiki/Galactic_Senate "Galactic Senate"), and pursued [interplanetary](/wiki/Planet "Planet") criminals across [the galaxy](/wiki/The_galaxy "The galaxy").[[2]](#cite_note-UltimateSW-2) Whereas the [Sith](/wiki/Sith "Sith")—the [historic](/wiki/Timeline_of_galactic_history "Timeline of galactic history") enemies of the Jedi Order—harnessed the [dark side of the Force](/wiki/Dark_side_of_the_Force "Dark side of the Force") for power,[[46]](#cite_note-DB:Sith-46) the Jedi followed the ways of the [light side of the Force](/wiki/Light_side_of_the_Force "Light side of the Force").[[4]](#cite_note-DB:Order-4) The [Jedi Code](/wiki/Jedi_Code "Jedi Code"),[[20]](#cite_note-TSWB-20) along with a collection of [other foundational texts](/wiki/Sacred_Jedi_texts "Sacred Jedi texts"),[[18]](#cite_note-Episode_VIII-18) guided the Jedi way of life, governing the behavior of individual Jedi to the philosophy and [training](/wiki/Jedi_training "Jedi training") regimen of the Order as a whole.[[20]](#cite_note-TSWB-20) Though the Jedi worshipped no specific [deity](/wiki/Deity "Deity"), the [Chosen One](/wiki/Chosen_One "Chosen One") played an important role in Jedi prophecy and mythology.[[47]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-47) According to [Padawan](/wiki/Padawan "Padawan") [Matthea Cathley](/wiki/Matthea_Cathley "Matthea Cathley"), the Jedi worked better as a group instead of on their own;[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) indeed, Jedi Knight [Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Obi-Wan Kenobi") once reflected that, as part of the Order, he was stronger than if he was on his own.[[42]](#cite_note-Obi-Wan_and_Anakin_5-42)

The virtues of the Order included compassion, generosity, peaceful resolution,[[49]](#cite_note-Catalyst-49) and spreading justice.[[50]](#cite_note-Convergence-50) As spelled out directly in one version of the Jedi Code, a Jedi was not supposed to act in pursuit of personal power or wealth, instead acting only with the goals of finding knowledge and enlightenment.[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) Further Jedi goals included finding balance[[51]](#cite_note-Age_Qui-Gon-51) and protecting others in a just fashion[[50]](#cite_note-Convergence-50) as part of a selfless quest to aid their fellow beings.[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) Nonetheless, Jedi needed to understand they were, like all people, imperfect and needed to always learn to be better.[[50]](#cite_note-Convergence-50) Like anyone, a Jedi could also be scared, but a Jedi was supposed to not run from their fears[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) or let those fears consume them,[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) instead facing those fears directly and remaining confident in the knowledge the Force was with them.[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) In short, their duties as servants of light and the Republic could be summed up as teachers, explorers, diplomats, and warriors.[[28]](#cite_note-Light_of_the_Jedi-28)

The Jedi were instructed in the ways of the Order and the Force; as their knowledge grew, each member progressed through several different ranks. With the exception of [Anakin Skywalker](/wiki/Anakin_Skywalker "Anakin Skywalker"), prospective Jedi were identified a short [time](/wiki/Time "Time") after [birth](/wiki/Reproduction "Reproduction") by the quantity of [midi-chlorians](/wiki/Midi-chlorian "Midi-chlorian") in their [blood](/wiki/Blood "Blood"), a factor which indicated the level of a subject's Force-sensitivity.[[25]](#cite_note-Episode_I-25) Many of these children were listed within Jedi [holocrons](/wiki/Holocron "Holocron") before being identified by the Order. Training began at the level of the [Jedi Initiate](/wiki/Jedi_Initiate "Jedi Initiate"); at some point in their training, [younglings](/wiki/Youngling "Youngling") were expected to find their own [Kyber crystal](/wiki/Kyber_crystal "Kyber crystal")—the heart of the [lightsaber](/wiki/Lightsaber "Lightsaber"),[[52]](#cite_note-DB:Kyber-52) a distinctive and elegant weapon of the Jedi[[53]](#cite_note-DB:Lightsaber-53)—in order to pass an ancient rite of passage known as [The Gathering](/wiki/Gathering "Gathering").[[54]](#cite_note-DB:Ilum-54)

 [![Padawans were assigned to fully-trained Jedi, such as Knights or Masters, in order to complete their training in the Jedi arts.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/03/Coruscantsunset.png/revision/latest?cb=20130118051000) [![Padawans were assigned to fully-trained Jedi, such as Knights or Masters, in order to complete their training in the Jedi arts.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/03/Coruscantsunset.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20130118051000)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/03/Coruscantsunset.png/revision/latest?cb=20130118051000) 

Padawans were assigned to fully-trained Jedi, such as Knights or Masters, in order to complete their training in the Jedi arts.

 

Younglings who succeeded in their trials graduated to the level of Padawan, the apprentice of a more experienced member of the Order. In accordance with the Jedi Code, a Master could instruct only one student in the ways of the Force at any given time. The [Padawan braid](/wiki/Padawan_braid "Padawan braid"), a symbol that represented a Jedi apprentice's status in the Order, was worn in the [hair](/wiki/Hair "Hair")[[25]](#cite_note-Episode_I-25) or head,[[55]](#cite_note-TCWFilm-55) depending on the Padawan's [species](/wiki/Species "Species").[[25]](#cite_note-Episode_I-25)[[56]](#cite_note-TWJ-56) The braid was removed when a Padawan ascended to the rank of Jedi Knight or in the case of [banishment](/wiki/Exile_(punishment) "Exile (punishment)") from the Order's ranks.[[57]](#cite_note-Wrong_Jedi_Ep_Gallery-57)

The [Jedi Trials](/wiki/Jedi_Trials "Jedi Trials") were a series of tests that ultimately determined whether a Padawan was worthy of the rank of Jedi Knight.[[25]](#cite_note-Episode_I-25) After becoming a full-fledged member of the Order, a Jedi could choose to adopt a Padawan of their own as part of the Order's tradition in training the next generation of Jedi.[[55]](#cite_note-TCWFilm-55) Teaching the ways of the Force to the next generation of Jedi was considered one of the greatest honors in the Order, its existence and traditions perpetuated through "a cycle of training and education."[[20]](#cite_note-TSWB-20) The [Eye of the Nihil](/wiki/Eye_of_the_Nihil "Eye of the Nihil"), [Marchion Ro](/wiki/Marchion_Ro "Marchion Ro"), believed that being structured into an order gave Jedi an advantage; in addition to tapping into the Force, any Jedi could tap into their Order to find confidence and structure. Being part of a united group made it so individual Jedi were willing to make large–scale decisions, which they believed would spread their light throughout the galaxy. In effect, a Jedi was not merely strong and bold because they could use the Force. Instead, being part of the overall Jedi Order helped them grow to embody those traits.[[28]](#cite_note-Light_of_the_Jedi-28)

 [![Comprised of twelve Jedi Masters, the Jedi High Council was the governing body of the Jedi Order.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5c/Jedicouncil2.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20160128232159) [![Comprised of twelve Jedi Masters, the Jedi High Council was the governing body of the Jedi Order.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5c/Jedicouncil2.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20160128232159)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5c/Jedicouncil2.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20160128232159) 

Comprised of twelve Jedi Masters, the Jedi High Council was the governing body of the Jedi Order.

 

The most powerful and legendary Jedi held the rank of Jedi Master[[58]](#cite_note-DB:Yoda-58) once they had proven themself worthy of the independence[[28]](#cite_note-Light_of_the_Jedi-28) and station granted by the title. Again with the exception of Skywalker, the [Jedi High Council](/wiki/Jedi_High_Council "Jedi High Council")[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19)—the highest governing body of the Order[[2]](#cite_note-UltimateSW-2)—consisted of Masters throughout the history of the Order.[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) Among the High Council, the title of [Grand Master](/wiki/Grand_Master "Grand Master") was conferred on the oldest and wisest member of their group,[[59]](#cite_note-UFC-59) while the Council's leadership rested with the [Master of the Order](/wiki/Master_of_the_Order "Master of the Order").[[3]](#cite_note-Rise_of_the_Separatists-3)

The Jedi Order in its capacity as a peacekeeping force of the Republic[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8) vowed allegiance to the Galactic Senate and [democracy](/wiki/Democracy "Democracy").[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) As an "extension" of the Republic's [Judiciary branch](/wiki/Judicial_Department "Judicial Department"),[[20]](#cite_note-TSWB-20) the Order was under the legal jurisdiction of the Senate,[[60]](#cite_note-Obi-Wan_&_Anakin_1-60) and as leader of the Senate,[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) the [Supreme Chancellor](/wiki/Supreme_Chancellor "Supreme Chancellor") had the privilege to make requests of the Order.[[60]](#cite_note-Obi-Wan_&_Anakin_1-60) However, this prerogative did not give the chancellor direct authority over the Order, which was legally under senatorial oversight. According to [Sheev Palpatine](/wiki/Darth_Sidious "Darth Sidious"), the [Office of the Chancellor](/wiki/Office_of_the_Chancellor "Office of the Chancellor") would become a [dictatorship](/wiki/Dictatorship "Dictatorship") if the Order was forced to comply with orders from the Republic head of state.[[61]](#cite_note-Obi-Wan_&_Anakin_4-61)

### Locations[]

:   "*The most famous of the Jedi temples, located on Coruscant, served as the home of the Jedi High Council and the vast library of data known as the Jedi Archives.*"
:   ―Luke Skywalker[[62]](#cite_note-Secrets_of_the_Jedi-62)

 [![The first Jedi Temple was built on a sacred island of Ahch-To.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/68/First_Jedi_Temple_TLJ.png/revision/latest?cb=20180509045418) [![The first Jedi Temple was built on a sacred island of Ahch-To.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/68/First_Jedi_Temple_TLJ.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20180509045418)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/68/First_Jedi_Temple_TLJ.png/revision/latest?cb=20180509045418) 

The first Jedi Temple was built on a sacred island of Ahch-To.

 

[Jedi temples](/wiki/Jedi_temple "Jedi temple") served as places of worship, training schools, and repositories of knowledge for the Jedi Order.[[62]](#cite_note-Secrets_of_the_Jedi-62) The [first Jedi Temple](/wiki/First_Jedi_Temple "First Jedi Temple") was built atop a [sacred island](/wiki/Temple_Island "Temple Island") on [Ahch-To](/wiki/Ahch-To "Ahch-To")[[63]](#cite_note-Ahch-To_Jedi_Temple_Databank-63) tens of thousands of years before the [First Order-Resistance War](/wiki/First_Order-Resistance_War "First Order-Resistance War").[[64]](#cite_note-Constructed_date-64) The temple rose high above the surrounding sea, and was worn down by erosion and time. Some signs of its past remained, however, such as mosaics and an ancient [meditation](/wiki/Meditation "Meditation") ledge.[[63]](#cite_note-Ahch-To_Jedi_Temple_Databank-63) One such mosaic depicted the Prime Jedi in a state of meditation; the same mosaic symbolized the nature of the Force as a duality between the dark side and the light.[[65]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-65)

 [![During the era of the Galactic Republic, the Jedi Order made its home in the Jedi Grand Temple on Coruscant.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9f/JediTemple_cloudysky.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20140802205911) [![During the era of the Galactic Republic, the Jedi Order made its home in the Jedi Grand Temple on Coruscant.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9f/JediTemple_cloudysky.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20140802205911)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9f/JediTemple_cloudysky.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20140802205911) 

During the era of the Galactic Republic, the Jedi Order made its home in the Jedi Grand Temple on Coruscant.

 

The Jedi Order made its home in the [Jedi Grand Temple](/wiki/Imperial_Palace "Imperial Palace") on [Coruscant](/wiki/Coruscant "Coruscant"),[[16]](#cite_note-DB:JediTemple-16) the [capital](/wiki/Capital "Capital") world of the Galactic Republic.[[66]](#cite_note-DB:Coruscant-66) Over the millennia, the Temple served as the central hub of all Jedi activities in the galaxy; it was a school, a monastery, and the headquarters of the Jedi High Council.[[16]](#cite_note-DB:JediTemple-16) As a school, the Temple was the largest active Jedi training center in the galaxy[[2]](#cite_note-UltimateSW-2) where younglings trained to become Padawans and ultimately full-fledged Jedi Knights. The [Jedi Archives](/wiki/Jedi_Archives "Jedi Archives"), the source of all knowledge accumulated by the Order, was located inside of the Temple.[[67]](#cite_note-Locations_Gallery-67)

As the symbol of the Order, the Temple signified the Order's status in galactic affairs.[[68]](#cite_note-TCaJ-68) While access to the Temple was not restricted to just the Jedi, all non-Jedi personnel were required to undergo compulsory entry tests before becoming employed at the Temple. Those who worked in the Temple often dedicated their whole life to serving the Order.[[69]](#cite_note-Sabotage-69) Having sustained extensive damage during the fall of the Jedi, the Temple was renovated and renamed as the Imperial Palace,[[16]](#cite_note-DB:JediTemple-16) with only the original structure's corpse and five skyscraping towers remaining intact.[[70]](#cite_note-Tarkin-70) In addition to the Temple on Coruscant, the Order maintained several ancient temples spread across the galaxy.[[71]](#cite_note-PotJ-71) Jedi understood they were connected to the entire galaxy through their Order, seeing the galaxy itself as their home instead of a singular location as deserving that term.[[50]](#cite_note-Convergence-50)

 [![The Jedi Temple on Ilum was used for a sacred ritual known as The Gathering.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/02/Jedi_Temple_Ilum.png/revision/latest?cb=20150107023326) [![The Jedi Temple on Ilum was used for a sacred ritual known as The Gathering.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/02/Jedi_Temple_Ilum.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20150107023326)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/02/Jedi_Temple_Ilum.png/revision/latest?cb=20150107023326) 

The Jedi Temple on Ilum was used for a sacred ritual known as The Gathering.

 

One [ancient temple](/wiki/Lothal_Jedi_Temple "Lothal Jedi Temple") was located on [Lothal](/wiki/Lothal "Lothal"), and was only accessible if both the Master and Padawan were present. The Lothal temple was where Padawans were sent to confront their fear without the support of the Masters, some of whom ultimately died while waiting for their students who never returned, leaving the temple's antechambers littered with their skeletal remains.[[71]](#cite_note-PotJ-71) Other Jedi enclaves included the [Temple of Eedit](/wiki/Temple_of_Eedit "Temple of Eedit") on [Devaron](/wiki/Devaron "Devaron"),[[72]](#cite_note-Monster-72)[[73]](#cite_note-weapon-jedi-73) the [Temple](/wiki/Jedi_Temple_(Vrogas_Vas) "Jedi Temple (Vrogas Vas)") of [Vrogas Vas](/wiki/Vrogas_Vas "Vrogas Vas"),[[74]](#cite_note-SW9-74) and the [Temple](/wiki/Jedi_Temple_(Ilum) "Jedi Temple (Ilum)") of [Ilum](/wiki/Ilum "Ilum") where younglings were sent to participate in The Gathering.[[54]](#cite_note-DB:Ilum-54) The Jedi Order established smaller outposts at various locations around the galaxy, including [one](/wiki/Elphrona_Outpost "Elphrona Outpost") on [Elphrona](/wiki/Elphrona "Elphrona"). These outposts dated as far back as the High Republic Era and the great Jedi spread across the galaxy that saw them work alongside various communities. It contained various artifacts that were important to the history of the Jedi.[[75]](#cite_note-Rise_of_Kylo_Ren_2-75)

While Ilum was regarded as the most sacred planet to the Jedi Order,[[54]](#cite_note-DB:Ilum-54) the [desert](/wiki/Desert "Desert") [moon](/wiki/Moon "Moon") [Jedha](/wiki/Jedha "Jedha")—a holy site and home to one of the first civilizations that explored the nature of the Force[[76]](#cite_note-DB:Jedha-76)—was considered a spiritual home of the Jedi.[[77]](#cite_note-SlashFilm_Jedha-77) Like Ilum,[[54]](#cite_note-DB:Ilum-54) Jedha contained the kyber [crystals](/wiki/Crystal "Crystal") that the Jedi used to create their lightsaber.[[78]](#cite_note-Jedha_LS-78) It was also a holy site for pilgrims throughout the galaxy, who sought spiritual guidance[[76]](#cite_note-DB:Jedha-76) in the [Holy City](/wiki/Jedha_City "Jedha City") of Jedha.[[79]](#cite_note-DB:Holy_City-79) At one time it was an important world to the Jedi.[[76]](#cite_note-DB:Jedha-76)

 [![The Jedi Temple on Ossus served as a training school for the apprentices of Jedi Master Luke Skywalker.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0f/Luke_Skywalkers_Jedi_temple.png/revision/latest?cb=20180421052313) [![The Jedi Temple on Ossus served as a training school for the apprentices of Jedi Master Luke Skywalker.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0f/Luke_Skywalkers_Jedi_temple.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20180421052313)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0f/Luke_Skywalkers_Jedi_temple.png/revision/latest?cb=20180421052313) 

The Jedi Temple on Ossus served as a training school for the apprentices of Jedi Master Luke Skywalker.

 

A number of Jedi sites could also be found on the planets [Tython](/wiki/Tython "Tython") and [Ossus](/wiki/Ossus "Ossus"), such as the [Jedi Temple of Tython](/wiki/Jedi_Temple_(Tython) "Jedi Temple (Tython)")[[6]](#cite_note-CL_2016-6) or the [First Temple](/wiki/First_Temple "First Temple") on Ossus.[[9]](#cite_note-Dooku:_Jedi_Lost-9) The Jedi maintained a connection to Tython, and one of their sacred [texts](/wiki/Book "Book") described "notable beasts of Tython."[[65]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-65) Ossus was also the location of the [Great Jedi Library](/wiki/Great_Jedi_Library "Great Jedi Library"), which was destroyed before the [Clone Wars](/wiki/Clone_Wars "Clone Wars")[[6]](#cite_note-CL_2016-6) and in complete ruins by the time of its rediscovery by [Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Luke_Skywalker "Luke Skywalker"). Despite this, Skywalker still located an original copy of the *[Rammahgon](/wiki/Rammahgon "Rammahgon")*, one of the sacred Jedi texts, on the planet.[[65]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-65) During the [New Republic Era](/wiki/New_Republic_Era "New Republic Era"), the [Jedi Temple of Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Jedi_Temple_of_Luke_Skywalker "Jedi Temple of Luke Skywalker") was constructed on[[80]](#cite_note-From_the_Desert_Comes_a_Stranger-80) Ossus[[81]](#cite_note-Shadow_of_the_Sith-81) with the goal of becoming a "great school" for future generations of students in the restored Jedi Order.[[80]](#cite_note-From_the_Desert_Comes_a_Stranger-80)

### General perception[]

#### Different traditions over time[]

 [![Compassion and non-attachment were regarded as essential to members of the Jedi Order](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/7d/EmerickAndKeeveHug-THRTrailOfShadows3.png/revision/latest?cb=20220116174531) [![Compassion and non-attachment were regarded as essential to members of the Jedi Order](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/7d/EmerickAndKeeveHug-THRTrailOfShadows3.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20220116174531)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/7d/EmerickAndKeeveHug-THRTrailOfShadows3.png/revision/latest?cb=20220116174531) 

Compassion and non-attachment were regarded as essential to members of the Jedi Order

 

With the galaxy changing as new threats emerged, the Jedi Order took on many forms and traditions over its life[[43]](#cite_note-Star_Wars_(2020)_20-43) in its mission to fight those threats.[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) As such, the particular way members of the Jedi Order interpreted the current form of its ideals impacted the way they interacted with the galactic population.[[82]](#cite_note-Dangerous_Debt-82) The High Republic Era was a time of greatly expanded Jedi activity, and the Order had many outposts throughout the galaxy.[[83]](#cite_note-The_Rise_of_Kylo_Ren_2-83) The Galactic Republic relied heavily on their role as guardians of peace and justice, to settle disputes through peaceful ways, to protect planetary leaders and senators.[[25]](#cite_note-Episode_I-25) With the Republic's rapid expansion and the Order's role in protecting that effort, the Jedi also established many new temples across the Outer Rim, keeping the buildings in line with the planetary cultures they found themselves in.[[28]](#cite_note-Light_of_the_Jedi-28) With many Jedi living amongst these communities[[84]](#cite_note-Yoda_interview-84) through such temples[[28]](#cite_note-Light_of_the_Jedi-28) or while out on their mission, the Jedi learned local customs[[85]](#cite_note-Yoda_1-85) and truly became part of the cultures[[84]](#cite_note-Yoda_interview-84) they protected.[[85]](#cite_note-Yoda_1-85)

By the time of the late Republic Era, the Order found itself shifting its focus more onto the galactic scale of the responsibilities required of the Order. In this era, the Jedi were more likely to focus on and spend their time on the galactic astropolitical scene and the bigger questions: stopping menaces, some before they even developed, and saving whole star systems at a time. Knowing that their decisions affected billions of lives, the Jedi Council regularly sent out Knights to report on the state of the various parts of the galaxy. However, as their duties amounted, several Jedi outposts were shut down to direct resources where the Republic needed the Jedi the most, and their withdrawal caused many people to abandon the settlements grown around the presence of the Order.[[86]](#cite_note-TLF-86)

While [Jedi Sentinels](/wiki/Jedi_Sentinel "Jedi Sentinel") still existed and made it their duty to work with the everyday people of the galaxy,[[87]](#cite_note-Endless_Vigil-87) Jedi Knights found it increasingly difficult to find time for personal interaction with the people of the galaxy, with many young Jedi often forgetting that concerns that seemed small on a galactic level were often huge for the individual. That was despite Master Yoda and other Council members' efforts to teach them to pay attention to the present and where they are. In effect,[[86]](#cite_note-TLF-86) the Jedi Order grew increasingly isolated from the galaxy at large, much to the concern of Jedi Master Qui-Gon Jinn, due to its shrinking number of outposts.[[88]](#cite_note-Living_Force_Reveal-88)

Focusing on galactic issues instead of remaining on a smaller scale, the Jedi thus were focused more and more on the future of the Republic. Secluded from the galaxy at large due to its headquarters on Coruscant,[[88]](#cite_note-Living_Force_Reveal-88) the Jedi Order was left adrift, not only because of its isolation but also how it had become heedless of strange changes within the Force.[[89]](#cite_note-Jedi_Temple_DB-89) While the Jedi still cared about the galaxy,[[86]](#cite_note-TLF-86) the Jedi stayed locked away[[84]](#cite_note-Yoda_interview-84) in their shrinking number of temples,[[86]](#cite_note-TLF-86) instead of remaining a part of local communities as they had in the High Republic Era.[[84]](#cite_note-Yoda_interview-84) Jinn and Master Yoda feared that, since many people of the galaxy saw and interacted with Jedi Knights less and less, they might start to believe or could be made to believe that the Order ceased to care about them. What with many of the Order's other outposts being shut down while the Temple on Coruscant remained,[[86]](#cite_note-TLF-86) Jinn pondered if the Order's headquarters sitting on Coruscant was a problem, reasoning it made them look like Republic warriors. While Yoda warned him that the Council would not agree with his concerns about Coruscant, Jinn even feared the Jedi themselves could fall into that viewpoint and lose the true meaning of what it meant to be a Jedi.[[51]](#cite_note-Age_Qui-Gon-51)

During the High Republic Era, the Order and the Jedi Council enabled Jedi who were drawn to solitary action to become "[Wayseekers](/wiki/Wayseeker "Wayseeker")"—Jedi who operated outside of the dictates of the Council[[90]](#cite_note-Into_the_Dark-90) to instead follow the Force on their own terms.[[91]](#cite_note-THR_7-91) Such a position was seemingly not permitted in the late Republic Era due to the defiance it showed towards the council.[[92]](#cite_note-Padawan_Novel-92) Wayseekers were still bound to the values of the Order, so their abilities and skills could not be used in the pursuit of selfish concerns.[[90]](#cite_note-Into_the_Dark-90)

Although they were not eager to be [soldiers](/wiki/Soldier "Soldier"),[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8) the Jedi many times found that other skills were not enough and so their role was to fight, indeed this was understood in the High Republic as a vital, though unfortunate role of a Jedi. They took military actions against the Sith,[[28]](#cite_note-Light_of_the_Jedi-28) lead soldiers against the Nihil,[[93]](#cite_note-The_High_Republic:_Tempest_Runner-93) and in the last years of the Republic reprised this office, became [generals](/wiki/General "General") of the [Republic Military](/wiki/Republic_Military "Republic Military") and fighting in the Clone Wars.[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) Even after the fall of the Order, Jedi like Luke Skywalker and Rey fought the darkness as the edge of the powers that opposed tyranny.[[94]](#cite_note-Episode_V-94)[[65]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-65)

#### Letting go[]

:   "*Strong passions are something we try to control within ourselves, as emotions can cloud our judgment, especially in stressful situations. They can blind us to the truth, and to the leading of the Force. That said, it would be foolish to suggest that a Jedi has no desires or interests. In fact, I would go so far as to say that it would be dangerous, leading only to complacency. Yes, I have a passion for learning and teaching. It is part of who I am. But I am also prepared to set such things aside at a moment's notice. My 'passions' must never be greater than my mission.*"
:   ―Master Stellan Gios[[95]](#cite_note-The_Rising_Storm-95)

 [![To be a Jedi was to let go: friends would live and pass on, but a Jedi could not allow their connection to give way to uncontrolled grief.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/38/FauxFuneral-Deception.png/revision/latest?cb=20130601230228) [![To be a Jedi was to let go: friends would live and pass on, but a Jedi could not allow their connection to give way to uncontrolled grief.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/38/FauxFuneral-Deception.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20130601230228)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/38/FauxFuneral-Deception.png/revision/latest?cb=20130601230228) 

To be a Jedi was to let go: friends would live and pass on, but a Jedi could not allow their connection to give way to uncontrolled grief.

 

Jedi Knights of all eras adhered to the Jedi Code, however, there were debates on how to follow its doctrines,[[47]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-47) and many Jedi developed their own personal understanding of them. One major concept was that of avoiding attachments, but different Jedi expressed different understandings of that rule.[[96]](#cite_note-Midnight_Horizon-96) [Padawan](/wiki/Padawan "Padawan") [Kevmo Zink](/wiki/Kevmo_Zink "Kevmo Zink") explained that the overall idea behind avoiding attachments was inspired by the Jedi Order's mission to the Force; if a Jedi was truly expected to work for the good of the entire galaxy, they could not tie themself down with one attachment, such as a romantic relationship with another being.[[97]](#cite_note-Path_of_Deceit-97)

If a Jedi did form such an attachment, the Order believed that the Jedi would not be as ready to spread the ideals of the light side across the galaxy because of the relationship, which the Order taught would be a distraction. It was hoped a Jedi Knight would only be bound to the Force and the Jedi Temple.[[97]](#cite_note-Path_of_Deceit-97) High Republic Era Jedi Master [Stellan Gios](/wiki/Stellan_Gios "Stellan Gios") explained that the Jedi tried to control their strong passions because the emotions one felt for those passions could cloud their judgement, particularly during a stressful moment. Still, he said it was wrong to deny that Jedi like himself had their own interests and desires; the task of a Jedi, he reasoned, was to not let those passions take control of their being.[[95]](#cite_note-The_Rising_Storm-95) As late Republic Era [Rael Averross](/wiki/Rael_Averross "Rael Averross") reasoned, the text of the [Jedi Code](/wiki/Jedi_Code "Jedi Code") forbid strong attachments that divided one's loyalties and compromised their emotions. As such, he further reasoned that a casual physical relationship—which he enjoyed with a woman named [Selbie](/wiki/Selbie "Selbie")—was only breaking the "letter" of the Jedi Code, not its actual binding spirit. While Averross's actions shocked his fellow Jedi Master [Qui-Gon Jinn](/wiki/Qui-Gon_Jinn "Qui-Gon Jinn"), Averross defended himself and pointed out how Jinn had made an actual violation of the Jedi Code in his past via a relationship with an [individual](/wiki/Unidentified_individual "Unidentified individual"), much to Jinn's pain. Jinn himself maintained fond memories of that past relationship despite having moved on to continue his life as a Jedi.[[98]](#cite_note-Master_Apprentice-98)

During the High Republic Era, according to Master [Kantam Sy](/wiki/Kantam_Sy "Kantam Sy")'s viewpoint, there were many Jedi who twisted the notion non-attachment; to Sy, those who spoke of suppressing emotions, forsaking love and trying to numb themselves to discomfort were twisting Jedi teachings. Jedi like Sy and Grand Master [Yoda](/wiki/Yoda "Yoda") taught non-attachment or detachment, just like love, was to let go of something or someone when the time called for it, instead of allowing oneself to be ruled by the need to possess.[[96]](#cite_note-Midnight_Horizon-96) Indeed, close friendships were respected and valued throughout the Jedi Order,[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) but a Jedi needed to understand they could lose those they cared for and thus would need to let go,[[96]](#cite_note-Midnight_Horizon-96) instead of letting their grief consume them.[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19)

That belief tied into the Jedi Order's beliefs on death; according to the Jedi, an individual became one with the Force upon death because they transferred into the [Cosmic Force](/wiki/Cosmic_Force "Cosmic Force"), which, in turn, generated the [Living Force](/wiki/Living_Force "Living Force"). As High Republic Era Jedi Master [Obratuk Glii](/wiki/Obratuk_Glii "Obratuk Glii") explained, he was still allowed to miss his former apprentices, but he knew they were still with him through the Force, generating a joy within him that his fellows had become part of the Force. Furthermore, he declared it meant he could not be scared of his own mortality.[[99]](#cite_note-HRA_7-99) As selfless defenders of peace and justice,[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) Jedi were also willing to lay down their own lives in defense of others[[100]](#cite_note-Supply_Lines-100) and did not fear death. Instead, a Jedi was supposed to always put the needs of other people before their own needs.[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) While Glii's commentary argued that Jedi could grieve to a certain degree so long as it did not consume them,[[99]](#cite_note-HRA_7-99) Padawan Matthea Cathley, who also lived during the High Republic Era, once thought to herself that Jedi did not grieve, but her thought was based in the understanding of not losing oneself to attachment over a deceased individual. Even then, she noted not grieving was hard in practice. Cathley also once claimed that Jedi did not get scared, but she later accepted that, like everyone, Jedi did indeed have fears and they needed to face them; as she put it, there was no shame in admitting when she was scared, but it was her duty to face whatever spawned that fear.[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48)

 [![The Jedi Order taught its members to move beyond what they feared to lose, ensuring a Jedi did not cling onto the present in an ever-changing galaxy.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9d/YodaCouncilsAnakin-ROTS.png/revision/latest?cb=20130202024305) [![The Jedi Order taught its members to move beyond what they feared to lose, ensuring a Jedi did not cling onto the present in an ever-changing galaxy.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9d/YodaCouncilsAnakin-ROTS.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20130202024305)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9d/YodaCouncilsAnakin-ROTS.png/revision/latest?cb=20130202024305) 

The Jedi Order taught its members to move beyond what they feared to lose, ensuring a Jedi did not cling onto the present in an ever-changing galaxy.

 

As such, a Jedi needed to be careful with their relationships[[97]](#cite_note-Path_of_Deceit-97) so as to not let attachment, and the naturally ensuing fear of losing those attachments, consume them.[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) It was not that a Jedi was not allowed to feel romantic love, as it was understood such feelings were natural, but a Jedi were not supposed to enter into a romantic relationship. It was essential for a Jedi Knight to make the right choice for the Order and not neglect their Jedi duties in the favor of their beloved, even if that would mean the end of the relationship.[[101]](#cite_note-The_Rise_of_Clovis-101)[[102]](#cite_note-VoT-102) As Zink explained, a Jedi was able to use the Force to direct themselves through the tides of strong emotions and learn what the underlining motivations of those feelings were. With that, a Jedi would not be ruled by their passions, but instead could make tactical decisions with a better understanding of their own mindset.[[97]](#cite_note-Path_of_Deceit-97)

For some outsiders, as such, the Jedi teaching on the matter often misinterpreted, believed the Jedi to be distant and seemingly unconcerned about the lives of those they were to protect[[82]](#cite_note-Dangerous_Debt-82) and that "love" was forbidden for a Jedi.[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8) The actions of some emotionally distant Jedi Knights did little to help that misconception:[[82]](#cite_note-Dangerous_Debt-82)[[50]](#cite_note-Convergence-50) during the days of the High Republic, a Jedi Knight saved the lives of a starship crew, including the young [Axel Greylark](/wiki/Axel_Greylark "Axel Greylark"), but needed to drag the badly injured boy away from [his father](/wiki/Lexxir_Greylark "Lexxir Greylark"), trapped under the rubble, thus leaving him behind. The Jedi told him that what happened was the will of the Force, something that left Greylark baffled. Years later, when he recounted the incident to Jedi Knight [Gella Nattai](/wiki/Gella_Nattai "Gella Nattai") and how the Knight later forgot his face, he concluded that one grieving boy in a galaxy full of them was nothing, but Nattai affirmed to Greylark that one grieving boy was everything.[[50]](#cite_note-Convergence-50)

Jedi of the High Republic Era displayed a great deal of emotional openness to those grieving[[103]](#cite_note-THR_(2021)_3-103) or upset[[104]](#cite_note-Trail_of_Shadows_3-104)—showing it in actions like offering a hug.[[103]](#cite_note-THR_(2021)_3-103)[[104]](#cite_note-Trail_of_Shadows_3-104) During the waning decades of the Republic, compassion was still meant to be central to a Jedi's life,[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8) with the non-attachment rule defined in theory as someone not meant to fearfully grasp on things and beings in a [universe](/wiki/Universe "Universe") ruled by change.[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8)[[101]](#cite_note-The_Rise_of_Clovis-101)[[105]](#cite_note-Kanan_1-105)[[106]](#cite_note-Jedi_Crash-106)[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) However, the actions of a Jedi appearing not to care could damage the entire Order's reputation[[82]](#cite_note-Dangerous_Debt-82) or result in that Jedi failing to help someone who needed support. Jedi Knight [Iskat Akaris](/wiki/Thirteenth_Sister "Thirteenth Sister") found a lack of support amongst the Jedi as she grappled with her insecurities during the late Republic Era.[[107]](#cite_note-Rise_of_the_Red_Blade-107)

During the Clone Wars, amid an [incident](/wiki/Senate_hostage_crisis "Senate hostage crisis") on Coruscant in which the Jedi attempted to recapture the [Hutt](/wiki/Hutt "Hutt") [crime lord](/wiki/Crime_lord "Crime lord") [Ziro Desilijic Tiure](/wiki/Ziro_Desilijic_Tiure "Ziro Desilijic Tiure"), a Jedi was forced to redirect a transport to ensure it avoided hitting a platform of people, but the redirected ship instead crashed into the [Martez family](/wiki/Martez_family "Martez family") apartment. Two children—[Trace](/wiki/Trace_Martez "Trace Martez") and [Rafa Martez](/wiki/Rafa_Martez "Rafa Martez")—became orphans in the incident with the demise of their parents in the crash. The Jedi in question then failed to properly explain herself in a compassionate matter, trying to assure both that she had needed to make a choice but that the Force would still be with them, a phrase that meant nothing to the two girls.[[82]](#cite_note-Dangerous_Debt-82)

 [![For Luke Skywalker, surrendering to one's attachments was to forsake the ways of the Jedi Order.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/ac/LukeYodasSecondLightsaber-FromTheDesertComesAStranger.png/revision/latest?cb=20220203035839) [![For Luke Skywalker, surrendering to one's attachments was to forsake the ways of the Jedi Order.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/ac/LukeYodasSecondLightsaber-FromTheDesertComesAStranger.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20220203035839)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/ac/LukeYodasSecondLightsaber-FromTheDesertComesAStranger.png/revision/latest?cb=20220203035839) 

For Luke Skywalker, surrendering to one's attachments was to forsake the ways of the Jedi Order.

 

Luke Skywalker affirmed the Jedi Order's commitment to non-attachment since the early days of his efforts to rebuild it.[[80]](#cite_note-From_the_Desert_Comes_a_Stranger-80) However, he also told his sister, [Leia Organa](/wiki/Leia_Skywalker_Organa_Solo "Leia Skywalker Organa Solo"), that she could still be [married](/wiki/Marriage "Marriage") to [Han Solo](/wiki/Han_Solo "Han Solo") if she joined the Order.[[108]](#cite_note-The_Princess_and_the_Scoundrel-108) Due to his unorthodox training in the Jedi arts, Skywalker sought to provide the next generation of Jedi with a more conventional path to knighthood.[[62]](#cite_note-Secrets_of_the_Jedi-62) As the last Jedi of his era,[[75]](#cite_note-Rise_of_Kylo_Ren_2-75) Skywalker found comfort through adherence to the Jedi way, having largely isolated himself from his friends while rebuilding the Order.[[81]](#cite_note-Shadow_of_the_Sith-81) In addition, [the Armorer](/wiki/The_Armorer "The Armorer")—a [Mandalorian](/wiki/Mandalorian "Mandalorian") who was familiar with Jedi history—stated that the Jedi were required to sacrifice personal attachments in order to master the ways of the Force.[[109]](#cite_note-Chapter_5:_Return_of_the_Mandalorian-109) While in the process of training [Grogu](/wiki/Din_Grogu "Din Grogu"), Skywalker informed his apprentice that giving into attachments to those whom he loved was to forsake the way of the Jedi.[[80]](#cite_note-From_the_Desert_Comes_a_Stranger-80)

#### Views on the lightsaber[]

 [![Indara chose to only draw her lightsaber as a last resort.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d2/Indara-JSW.png/revision/latest?cb=20251225033348) [![Indara chose to only draw her lightsaber as a last resort.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d2/Indara-JSW.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20251225033348)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d2/Indara-JSW.png/revision/latest?cb=20251225033348) 

Indara chose to only draw her lightsaber as a last resort.

 

:   "*I realized something. Something important. A Jedi isn't his lightsaber. A lightsaber is just a tool. A Jedi is someone who uses the Force to bring light to the galaxy. To protect people and push back darkness. That particular lightsaber… the one I lost… I don't need it. It was my father's… but I'm not sure how I feel about that anymore. I'm going to be a Jedi. Even if I never see that lightsaber again.*"
:   ―Luke Skywalker[[110]](#cite_note-SW_2020_4-110)

During the history of the Jedi Order, the lightsaber considered to be the Jedi's only true ally in battle.[[111]](#cite_note-Test_of_Strength-111) Beyond its existence as a weapon,[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8) however, the lightsaber was a symbol of care to the Jedi; as explained by Jedi Knight Obi-Wan Kenobi, the blade represented the care with which they approached and wielded their gifts, further serving as a message to their opponents and representing something that needed great skill and training to wield. In choosing a rather limited weapon, Kenobi explained, the lightsaber was also the symbol of their role and duty as protectors, not destroyers. Further reasoned by Kenobi to be a tool that showed the Jedi could be more powerful but openly chose not to be, the lightsaber represented a Jedi's duty to stand tall against darkness.[[112]](#cite_note-The_Lesson_Anakin-112) While the phrase "this weapon is your life" was popular during the late Republic Era,[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8)[[113]](#cite_note-Hostage_Crisis-113) a Jedi—as exemplified by the High Republic Era[[114]](#cite_note-Cataclysm-114) and Kenobi's speech[[112]](#cite_note-The_Lesson_Anakin-112)—needed to be more than their lightsaber.[[114]](#cite_note-Cataclysm-114) Indeed, after the Order's fall, Luke Skywalker came to realize that a Jedi was not their lightsaber and instead the duty he was tasked with was something beyond a single weapon. Faced with either needing to rescue his friend [Leia Organa](/wiki/Leia_Skywalker_Organa_Solo "Leia Skywalker Organa Solo") or continue looking for his lightsaber on [Cloud City](/wiki/Cloud_City "Cloud City"), Skywalker came to his decision and left to help his friend.[[110]](#cite_note-SW_2020_4-110)

 [![The High Republic Era saw a greater variance in lightsaber color than just green and blue lightsabers.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/06/KhofarMissionJedi-OfficialAcolyteX.png/revision/latest?cb=20240621005206) [![The High Republic Era saw a greater variance in lightsaber color than just green and blue lightsabers.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/06/KhofarMissionJedi-OfficialAcolyteX.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/275?cb=20240621005206)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/06/KhofarMissionJedi-OfficialAcolyteX.png/revision/latest?cb=20240621005206) 

The High Republic Era saw a greater variance in lightsaber color than just green and blue lightsabers.

 

The High Republic Era would also see a greater variance in lightsaber color[[115]](#cite_note-THR_8-115)[[116]](#cite_note-Trailer-116) and hilt design[[117]](#cite_note-Shadows_1-117) than the Jedi of the late Republic. During the late Republic era, Jedi largely wielded blue or green lightsabers with simple silver hilts.[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8) A shift in lightsaber design could be seen in the High Republic Era: the [Nihil conflict](/wiki/Nihil_conflict "Nihil conflict") saw the Jedi Order implement the [Guardian Protocols](/wiki/Guardian_Protocols "Guardian Protocols") and prepare for greater conflict, during which the High Council knew Jedi could lose their blade and be forced to quickly replace it. Rather than have Jedi spend time building elaborated hilts, the Council reasoned that speed and effectiveness was of the essence and that a ready supply of lightsabers was something the Order needed. As such, the Council ordered Jedi to only construct [battle sabers](/wiki/Battle_saber "Battle saber"), hilts with a simple design[[117]](#cite_note-Shadows_1-117) like those seen in the late Republic Era.[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8) Even then, Jedi active in the later High Republic Era still had a wider variance in lightsaber color[[116]](#cite_note-Trailer-116) than the blue and green-filled Order of the late Republic.[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8) While each individual Jedi built their own lightsaber as a youngling to their own specifications, allowing for a degree of individuality in hilt design even during the late Republic Era,[[111]](#cite_note-Test_of_Strength-111) groupings of Jedi of that time were largely defined by cylindrical silver hilts of an overall similar design, with those hilts mainly producing green or blue blades.[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8)

#### Who gets to join[]

:   "*Wait— you mean, I can be a Jedi?*"  
    "*Study you should, the Farseeker Lyr. No great power had he, yet from his ink sprang some of the Jedi's greatest texts. For though the Jedi and the Force are one, the Force is not what a Jedi makes.*"  
    "*Then what makes a Jedi?*"  
    "*That is something only you can answer.*"
:   ―Lohim Nara and Yoda during the High Republic Era[[118]](#cite_note-What_a_Jedi_Makes-118)

During the High Republic Era, when the young boy [Lohim Nara](/wiki/Lohim_Nara "Lohim Nara") spoke to Grand Master Yoda about his life-long desire to join the Order, he confessed that he had faked his Force-sensitivity and midi-chlorian count, but Yoda told the boy of how the Force was not the sole answer to what a Jedi was. Yoda spoke of how the Force existed in all life forms and how, if he wanted to be someone worthy of the name Jedi, he could not dwell on what he did not have. He also told the boy not to worry about being "too old" to become a youngling, stating that he was still learning at over six hundred years old. While Yoda seemed to admit the boy could not be a Jedi Knight due to his age, he noted that other professions helped the Order and offered him a role as a guardian of the Temple after Nara realized he had a mentor in [Reina Bilass](/wiki/Reina_Bilass "Reina Bilass").[[118]](#cite_note-What_a_Jedi_Makes-118)

 [![Yoda served as a Jedi Master for centuries and thus was present to watch as the Jedi Order changed with the galaxy.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/4b/Kenobi_and_Yoda_Turret_Room.png/revision/latest?cb=20190526110603) [![Yoda served as a Jedi Master for centuries and thus was present to watch as the Jedi Order changed with the galaxy.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/4b/Kenobi_and_Yoda_Turret_Room.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20190526110603)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/4b/Kenobi_and_Yoda_Turret_Room.png/revision/latest?cb=20190526110603) 

Yoda served as a Jedi Master for centuries and thus was present to watch as the Jedi Order changed with the galaxy.

 

However, later in its history, the Order proved reluctant but willing to bend their rules as the death of Jedi Master [Qui-Gon Jinn](/wiki/Qui-Gon_Jinn "Qui-Gon Jinn") and return of Sith convinced the Council to allow the young Anakin Skywalker to be trained, despite he was initially deemed too old.[[25]](#cite_note-Episode_I-25) Decades later, Yoda also chose to take Luke Skywalker as his apprentice after initially pointing out how old he was.[[94]](#cite_note-Episode_V-94) Alternatively, the Order of the High Republic also became a home for the young Force-sensitive [Zeen Mrala](/wiki/Zeen_Mrala-Talisola "Zeen Mrala-Talisola"), who did not train as a Jedi but became close to many Padawans and, despite Jedi regulations forbidding its members from engaging in romance, fell in love with Padawan [Lula Talisola](/wiki/Lula_Mrala-Talisola "Lula Mrala-Talisola").[[96]](#cite_note-Midnight_Horizon-96) Despite not being a Jedi, she was welcomed to train with the Padawans and their masters, with Talisola's master Kantam Sy helping her to control her anger.[[119]](#cite_note-THRA_12-119) Later, in order to find and save Talisola, Mrala realized that she was willing to join the ranks of the Jedi despite her age, although her realization came from how she figured certain Jedi rules would be bent due to the evolving Nihil conflict.[[96]](#cite_note-Midnight_Horizon-96)

The High Republic Era Order also maintained close ties with other Force orders, working as part of the [Convocation of the Force](/wiki/Convocation_of_the_Force "Convocation of the Force") on Jedha.[[97]](#cite_note-Path_of_Deceit-97) Through its ties to other orders, the Jedi brought rescued children who were "too old" to be trained as Jedi to Jedha, where they were taken in by other faiths.[[50]](#cite_note-Convergence-50) In the late Republic Era, the Jedi continued to help orphans find new homes, but there were instances where they failed to do so because of local law[[120]](#cite_note-The_Weapon-120) or their own non-attachment rule going so far it blurred the line between non-attachment and apathy, such as when a Jedi of the late Republic Era left Trace and Rafa Martez on their own after the deaths of their parents. Beyond those deaths being an indirect result of the Jedi's own actions, the Jedi's apparent lack of concern and the fact they simply left the two girls on their own created a distaste in both girls towards the Jedi Order, on whom they did not want to depend upon.[[82]](#cite_note-Dangerous_Debt-82)

#### Leaving the Order[]

:   "*The Jedi have been my family since I was a child, the Temple my home. But my future lies here, on Serenno* […] *I am the heir of Serenno. I will rebuild this planet, make it stronger. Not for the Republic. And not for the Jedi. But for the people. My people. I ask for you, and the Council, to respect my decision in this matter.*"  
    "*Hm. Saddened by your decision we are, but honor it we will.*"  
    "*Thank you. I will surrender my lightsaber to Master Kostana.*"  
    "*No. Necessary that will not be.*"  
    "*It is the weapon of a Jedi.*"  
    "*Which is why keep it you must. More than a name, a Jedi is. More than a title. Strong in the Force, you are. Guide you, it will. Guide us all, it must.*"
:   ―Dooku speaks to Yoda about his decision[[9]](#cite_note-Dooku:_Jedi_Lost-9)

While Grand Master Yoda once declared in the late Republic Era that a Jedi leaving the Order was a failure on the Order's part to keep that Jedi where they belonged, Jedi were permitted to leave the Jedi Order whenever they so chose without punishment,[[114]](#cite_note-Cataclysm-114) with Yoda accepting that fact, even if a Jedi leaving might sadden him. Should they feel it to be their calling, a former Jedi was even permitted to return to the Order. During the High Republic Era, one of Yoda's Padawans, Kantam Sy, walked away from the Jedi for over a year before returning when they met their soon-to-be Padawan [Lula Talisola](/wiki/Lula_Mrala-Talisola "Lula Mrala-Talisola"), who made Sy believe their place was with the Order. Jedi Master [Cohmac Vitus](/wiki/Cohmac_Vitus "Cohmac Vitus") was surprised Yoda would allow his Padawan to do a walkaway from the Order, but Sy believed Yoda knew it was necessary for them to find their place in the Order, with Sy at the time also thinking Yoda had seen it coming and thus was why he had held off on their Knighting.[[96]](#cite_note-Midnight_Horizon-96)

Twenty Jedi Masters who departed the Order became known as the "[Lost Twenty](/wiki/Lost_Twenty "Lost Twenty")" and were commemorated by busts located in the [Jedi Archives](/wiki/Jedi_Archives "Jedi Archives") of the Temple. Yoda believed the Lost needed to be remembered and honored, which enabled the Jedi to learn from the failings that caused them to depart. Still, he advised the Jedi not to live in the past just because prior members had departed. The twentieth of the Lost was [Dooku](/wiki/Dooku "Dooku"),[[121]](#cite_note-Absolutely_Everything-121) a former Padawan of Yoda who departed over issues with the Jedi and Republic. Despite his departure, Dooku was allowed to visit the Temple on Coruscant,[[122]](#cite_note-Padawan_novel-122) continued to have access to its Archives,[[123]](#cite_note-The_Sith_Lord-123) and was even allowed to retain possession of his lightsaber, with Yoda reasoning being a Jedi was more than a title and thus the weapon would still be of use to him.[[9]](#cite_note-Dooku:_Jedi_Lost-9)

#### Public image[]

##### Jedi unite for peace[]

:   "*The* Jedi Order *was strong, deeply seated into the galaxy's consciousness. They had a great temple in the heart of* Coruscant*, worked closely with* the Republic *and its chancellor for centuries. People made holodramas about them, wrote stories. The Jedi were…*celebrities*, and rightly so.*"
:   ―The Archivist[[124]](#cite_note-Crimson_Reign_3-124)

 [![The Jedi were committed in their duty as guardians of the Republic, but had no desire to be celebrated as such.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/eb/Jedi_Unite_for_Peace.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20161225090755) [![The Jedi were committed in their duty as guardians of the Republic, but had no desire to be celebrated as such.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/eb/Jedi_Unite_for_Peace.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20161225090755)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/eb/Jedi_Unite_for_Peace.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20161225090755) 

The Jedi were committed in their duty as guardians of the Republic, but had no desire to be celebrated as such.

 

The Jedi Order was regarded as a mysterious organization throughout its history.[[125]](#cite_note-Propaganda-125) The Order was ingrained in the public consciousness of the galaxy as a result of its strong ties to the government of the Galactic Republic,[[124]](#cite_note-Crimson_Reign_3-124) but was nonetheless inscrutable to the general public. However, those who encountered the Jedi were awed by their Force abilities.[[125]](#cite_note-Propaganda-125) Nevertheless, the Jedi were celebrities of their time, a status reflected by Jedi-themed [holodramas](/wiki/Holodrama "Holodrama") as well as stories written about the Order. [The Archivist](/wiki/The_Archivist "The Archivist"), a [historian](/wiki/Historian "Historian") who studied Jedi lore prior to joining [Crimson Dawn](/wiki/Crimson_Dawn "Crimson Dawn"), believed that to most people the Jedi exemplified the moral virtues that were affiliated with the light side of the Force, making them both loved and hated by the galaxy that they served.[[124]](#cite_note-Crimson_Reign_3-124)

During the High Republic, the Jedi actively worked to be part of local communities[[84]](#cite_note-Yoda_interview-84) in addition to helping them.[[85]](#cite_note-Yoda_1-85) However, the [Path of the Open Hand](/wiki/Path_of_the_Open_Hand "Path of the Open Hand") cult spread its influence by claiming all who used the Force were violating the energy field from its freedom, claiming that each use of the Force to solve a problem created an equal or worse problem elsewhere.[[126]](#cite_note-Perspective-126) The people of the planet [E'ronoh](/wiki/E%27ronoh "E'ronoh") were divided on the Jedi, with some believing they were miracle workers while others looked down on the Order as a group of Republic-backed outsiders. The arrival of the Path galvanized anti-Jedi sentiment on E'ronoh.[[50]](#cite_note-Convergence-50) The Path would, in time, evolve into the militant [Path of the Closed Fist](/wiki/Path_of_the_Closed_Fist "Path of the Closed Fist") that hoped to war with the Jedi.[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) Open Hand-adherent Path members[[114]](#cite_note-Cataclysm-114) and the Path's descendant movement,[[127]](#cite_note-Chronicles_of_the_Jedi-127) the [Elders of the Path](/wiki/Elders_of_the_Path "Elders of the Path"),[[128]](#cite_note-HRA_1-128) maintained their [anti-Jedi sentiment](/wiki/Anti-Jedi_sentiment "Anti-Jedi sentiment").[[114]](#cite_note-Cataclysm-114)[[128]](#cite_note-HRA_1-128) Open Hand [Elder](/wiki/Elder_(Path_of_the_Open_Hand) "Elder (Path of the Open Hand)") [Yulon Onning](/wiki/Yulon_Onning "Yulon Onning") abandoned the Closed Fist yet still hoped to see it triumph over the Jedi, whom he continued to see as "filth" and a group whose defeat would be a victory for the Open Hand.[[114]](#cite_note-Cataclysm-114) In the end, the Closed Fist would be succeeded by the [Nihil](/wiki/Nihil "Nihil"),[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) a group of marauders who waged war with the Jedi and Republic in their name of securing what they saw as their true freedom.[[28]](#cite_note-Light_of_the_Jedi-28)

In most situations, the Jedi were meant to lead rebuilding efforts after a battle had brought damage. However, the Holy Moon of Jedha presented an interesting case after the [Battle of Jedha](/wiki/Battle_of_Jedha "Battle of Jedha"):[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) in the past, the Jedi had once governed—and, in the opinion of some, "ruled over"—Jedha City[[129]](#cite_note-THR_2022_1-129) until the other religions who considered Jedha holy objected, believing that the Jedi were trying to depict themselves as the one true faith. The Jedi agreed to step down from their control,[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) but lingering [anti-Jedi sentiment](/wiki/Anti-Jedi_sentiment "Anti-Jedi sentiment") remained,[[129]](#cite_note-THR_2022_1-129) with one Jedha citizen once accusing the Jedi of always trying to control their lives.[[130]](#cite_note-THR_2022_5-130) That lingering anti-Jedi sentiment was used by the Path of the Open Hand to help bring the Battle of Jedha into being[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48) in [382 BBY](/wiki/382_BBY "382 BBY").[[17]](#cite_note-Timelines-17) After the battle, it was decided the [Guardians of the Whills](/wiki/Guardians_of_the_Whills "Guardians of the Whills") would serve as a steadying hand in the rebuilding effort instead of the Jedi because of still-lingering mistrust towards the Order on the part of Jedha citizens.[[48]](#cite_note-Path_of_Vengeance-48)

Public discontent with the Galactic Senate led to manifestations of anti-Jedi sentiment during the late Republic Era.[[131]](#cite_note-Choices-131) As an extension of the Galactic Republic's [Judicial Department](/wiki/Judicial_Department "Judicial Department"), the Jedi Order was subject to the authority of the Senate,[[20]](#cite_note-TSWB-20) and therefore, considered an instrument of the government's will. This belief was held both within the Senate[[132]](#cite_note-Justice-132) and without;[[131]](#cite_note-Choices-131) Senator [Dagonet](/wiki/Dagonet "Dagonet") said that the Jedi served the Senate,[[132]](#cite_note-Justice-132) and [Semage](/wiki/Semage "Semage") of [Raxus Secundus](/wiki/Raxus_Secundus "Raxus Secundus") accused them of being "lapdogs" for the Republic government. Hostility toward the Jedi extended to violent acts against members of the Order, such as Jedi Master [Katri](/wiki/Katri "Katri") who was killed by Semage and his guards.[[131]](#cite_note-Choices-131) Jedi Master Dooku became disenchanted with both the Senate and the Order, claiming that the Jedi served a "corrupt Senate" that had "failed the Republic"[[123]](#cite_note-The_Sith_Lord-123) in contrast to his former belief that the Jedi were servants of the Republic and its people.[[132]](#cite_note-Justice-132)

##### Clone War anti-Jedi views[]

###### Harmful propaganda[]

:   "*Emperor* Palpatine *rose to power because he made people afraid. He made people fear the* Jedi*. He called them* traitors*. He said they used their mystical powers to subvert democracy and peace, to cause war. It worked, possibly because as much as people* loved *the Jedi, they also* hated *them, on some level. It is hard to look at people who have become their* best selves*. It reminds you that* you have not*.*"
:   ―The Archivist[[124]](#cite_note-Crimson_Reign_3-124)

It is requested that this article section [be expanded](/wiki/Special:EditPage/:Jedi_Order "Special:EditPage/:Jedi Order"). *Please improve it in any way that you see fit, and remove this notice once the article section is more complete.*

During the Clone Wars, the [Commission for the Protection of the Republic](/wiki/Commission_for_the_Protection_of_the_Republic "Commission for the Protection of the Republic") (COMPOR) initially attempted to use the Order as an [instrument](/wiki/Jedi_Unite_for_Peace "Jedi Unite for Peace") for wartime [propaganda](/wiki/Propaganda "Propaganda"). This idea was discouraged by Supreme Chancellor Sheev Palpatine, who noted the Jedi's discomfort with their new role as generals in the Republic Military. COMPOR therefore focused its propaganda on the [clone troopers](/wiki/Clone_trooper "Clone trooper") who served under the Jedi's command, and as such the Jedi's contributions to the Republic war effort went largely unnoticed.[[125]](#cite_note-Propaganda-125)

 [![Anti-Jedi sentiment grew as a result of the Order's involvement in the Clone Wars.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/51/Deliver_Us_From_Jedi_Evil.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20180131040809) [![Anti-Jedi sentiment grew as a result of the Order's involvement in the Clone Wars.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/51/Deliver_Us_From_Jedi_Evil.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20180131040809)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/51/Deliver_Us_From_Jedi_Evil.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20180131040809) 

Anti-Jedi sentiment grew as a result of the Order's involvement in the Clone Wars.

 

The Jedi Order was vilified during the Clone Wars by elements within both the Republic and the Confederacy. The Separatists[[125]](#cite_note-Propaganda-125)—while, in total truth, being proponents of slavery at the secret direction of [Count](/wiki/Count "Count") [Dooku](/wiki/Dooku "Dooku")[[133]](#cite_note-Kidnapped-133)—accused the Jedi of hypocrisy, claiming that the Order supported the Republic's inhumane practice—as portrayed through Separatist propaganda—of using clones as a "[slave](/wiki/Slavery "Slavery") [army](/wiki/Army "Army")."
