Ahead of release, George Lucas claimed that *The Phantom Menace* depicted "the heyday of the Jedi," during which time there were thousands of Jedi and they acted as the "guardians of peace and justice in the galaxy, sort of like the old marshals out West."[[251]](#cite_note-251) Lucas felt he needed "to establish Jedi as what they were, which is sort of peacekeepers who moved through the galaxy to settle disputes."[[252]](#cite_note-An_Oral_History_of_Star_Wars:_Episode_I_The_Phantom_Menace-252) He described the Jedi as "warrior-monks who keep peace in the universe without resorting to violence."[[253]](#cite_note-:0-253) In the overall story of *Star Wars*, however, *The Phantom Menace* kicks off the [prequel trilogy](/wiki/Prequel_trilogy "Prequel trilogy"), which depicts the downfall of the Jedi Order.[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) Within [*Star Wars* Legends](/wiki/Star_Wars_Legends "Star Wars Legends")[[254]](#cite_note-Episode_III_novelization-254)[[255]](#cite_note-Darth_Plagueis-255) and canon, the prequel era overall represents a time in which the Jedi were losing their way,[[16]](#cite_note-DB:JediTemple-16)[[86]](#cite_note-TLF-86)[[56]](#cite_note-TWJ-56) with Episode II supporting that by featuring Yoda reflect on the increasing arrogance of even elder Jedi.[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8)

 [![The Jedi Order accepts a place of military leadership during the Clone Wars](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/3e/Jedi_Generals_Geonosis.png/revision/latest?cb=20180623160838) [![The Jedi Order accepts a place of military leadership during the Clone Wars](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/3e/Jedi_Generals_Geonosis.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20180623160838)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/3e/Jedi_Generals_Geonosis.png/revision/latest?cb=20180623160838) 

The Jedi Order accepts a place of military leadership during the Clone Wars

 

Rather than being "superheroes," Lucas noted how the Jedi Knights brought peace into the galaxy by "being ambassadors and trouble-shooters," who had the "moral authority" to keep the governments of the planets from becoming tyrannical or start wars. In that capacity, he said they had the power to "send the whole force of the Republic, which is 100,000 systems, so if you don't behave they can bring you up in front of the Senate" to "cut you off at the knees, politically."[[253]](#cite_note-:0-253) However, Episode II depicts the Jedi compromising their morals by taking up a military position in the newly formed Republic Military,[[8]](#cite_note-Episode_II-8) challenging the Order's philosophy of peacekeeping.[[102]](#cite_note-VoT-102) As acknowledged by Lucas, such means the audience couldn't see much of how Jedi Knights were supposed to operate, as the story quickly becomes the story of the Clone Wars.[[256]](#cite_note-256) As Lucas explained, "It's one of the conundrums of which there's a bunch of in my movies. You have to think it through. Are they going to stick with their moral rules and all be killed, which makes it irrelevant, or do they help save the Republic? They have good intentions, but they have been manipulated which was their downfall."[[253]](#cite_note-:0-253) The *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")* animated series produced under Lucas continued to study the themes of the Jedi Order and the road to its downfall.[[56]](#cite_note-TWJ-56)

*The Clone Wars* Supervising director [Dave Filoni](/wiki/Dave_Filoni "Dave Filoni") once noted that, in his mind at least, one of the story elements of the prequels was showing how the Jedi "almost forgot to care" and "[lacked] compassion" for Anakin Skywalker's situation, which leads to his fall to the dark side[[257]](#cite_note-Rebels_Recon_#3.02-257) and the destruction of their Order.[[19]](#cite_note-Episode_III-19) Filoni also pointed to Yoda's quote about Jedi arrogance in *Attack of the Clones*, saying Yoda “criticizes the Jedi in Episode II and says that they’ve become arrogant” and that “because they’ve become arrogant and very sure of themselves” they lack love and compassion.[[252]](#cite_note-An_Oral_History_of_Star_Wars:_Episode_I_The_Phantom_Menace-252)[[258]](#cite_note-258) Lucas, however, has said that Yoda was simply reminding Obi-Wan Kenobi that "arrogance exists in the older Jedi too, which is a way of warning Obi-Wan that he may be suffering the same hubris [as Anakin]."[[259]](#cite_note-:2-259)

Lucas also once stated that some people "didn't seem to understand the fact that Anakin is simply greedy"[[260]](#cite_note-The_Making_of_Star_Wars_Revenge_of_the_Sith-260) as the Jedi are "trained more than anything else to understand the transitional nature of life, that things are constantly changing and you can’t hold on to anything. You can love things but you can't be attached to them," which allows one to be "compassionate and loving and caring, but not be possessive and grabbing and holding on to things and trying to keep things the way they are." [[253]](#cite_note-:0-253) Anakin's issues are stemming not from some kind of failure of the Jedi, but from the fact that he started his training late in life, since if he would've been raised by the Jedi from a very early age, "he’d have been trained to love people but not to become attached to them."[[259]](#cite_note-:2-259)

### Sequel trilogy[]

Luke Skywalker's new generation of Jedi was first mentioned in the [2015](/wiki/2015 "2015") film [*Star Wars*: Episode VII *The Force Awakens*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VII_The_Force_Awakens "Star Wars: Episode VII The Force Awakens"),[[38]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-38) along with the film's [novelization](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens_(novelization) "Star Wars: The Force Awakens (novelization)")[[243]](#cite_note-TFA_novel-243) and [junior novelization](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens:_A_Junior_Novel "Star Wars: The Force Awakens: A Junior Novel").[[261]](#cite_note-TFA_junior-261) Further background details about the Jedi and their massacre, which saw the end of Luke's students, can be found in the reference book *[Star Wars: The Force Awakens: The Visual Dictionary](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens:_The_Visual_Dictionary "Star Wars: The Force Awakens: The Visual Dictionary")* by [Pablo Hidalgo](/wiki/Pablo_Hidalgo "Pablo Hidalgo").[[159]](#cite_note-tfa-TVD-159) On the contrary to what happened in the final films, George Lucas planned the Jedi Order to be restored by Luke Skywalker, who raised a new generation of Knights with the help of the surviving Jedi masters.[[253]](#cite_note-:0-253) Even then, however, Lucas's own plans for the sequel trilogy would have featured Skywalker in a dark state of mind, something of "a [Colonel Kurtz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apocalypse_Now "wikipedia:Apocalypse Now") type."[[262]](#cite_note-Art_of_TLJ-262)

### *The High Republic*[]

:   "*I think when people think about* The High Republic *down the road, they'll think about the Jedi. We've seen so many stories in* Star Wars *set during an era when they were in decline, or essentially gone, or bravely trying to rebuild themselves from almost nothing.* The High Republic*, at its heart, is an attempt to show an Order, and a Republic, at their strongest point. We've been hearing about what the Jedi meant to the galaxy for a thousand generations—we wanted to show it, and I think we succeeded.*"
:   ―Charles Soule[[263]](#cite_note-LongLive-263)

Writer [Cavan Scott](/wiki/Cavan_Scott "Cavan Scott") explained a theme of the *[Star Wars: The High Republic](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_High_Republic "Star Wars: The High Republic")* is seeing the Jedi live out amongst local communities, instead of being, comparatively, "locked away in their temples.[[84]](#cite_note-Yoda_interview-84) [Charles Soule](/wiki/Charles_Soule "Charles Soule") also explained, "The thing to know about The High Republic's Jedi is that the rules that exist in the prequel trilogy still exists. They still take the same vows, they still have the same feelings about it, but their understanding of the strength of the Order and flexibility within the Order and the interpretation of those rules ... they're more diffuse, I would say."[[264]](#cite_note-264)

According to actor [Charlie Barnett](/wiki/Charlie_Barnett "Charlie Barnett"), the High Republic Era-set series *[Star Wars: The Acolyte](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Acolyte "Star Wars: The Acolyte")* explores the theme of the Jedi Order having an ego due to it being their golden age, at which the Order was at its height. According to Barnett, this ego began to take control of the Jedi during the time of *The Acolyte*, paving the way for the Order's downfall.[[265]](#cite_note-Acolyte228-265)

[↑](#cite_ref-Constructed_date_64-0) *[Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker: The Visual Dictionary](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Rise_of_Skywalker:_The_Visual_Dictionary "Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker: The Visual Dictionary")* states that the first [Jedi Temple](/wiki/Jedi_temple "Jedi temple") was constructed on Ahch-To tens of thousands of [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") before the events of [*Star Wars*: Episode VIII *The Last Jedi*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VIII_The_Last_Jedi "Star Wars: Episode VIII The Last Jedi"). *Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker: The Visual Dictionary* places *Star Wars*: Episode VIII *The Last Jedi* in the same year as the events of [*Star Wars*: Episode VII *The Force Awakens*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VII_The_Force_Awakens "Star Wars: Episode VII The Force Awakens"), which *[Star Wars: Galactic Atlas](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galactic_Atlas "Star Wars: Galactic Atlas")* dates to [34 ABY](/wiki/34_ABY "34 ABY"). Therefore, the first Jedi Temple was constructed tens of thousands of years before 34 ABY. 65. ↑ [65.0](#cite_ref-TROS_VD_65-0) [65.1](#cite_ref-TROS_VD_65-1) [65.2](#cite_ref-TROS_VD_65-2) [65.3](#cite_ref-TROS_VD_65-3) [65.4](#cite_ref-TROS_VD_65-4) [65.5](#cite_ref-TROS_VD_65-5) [65.6](#cite_ref-TROS_VD_65-6) [65.7](#cite_ref-TROS_VD_65-7) *[Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker: The Visual Dictionary](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Rise_of_Skywalker:_The_Visual_Dictionary "Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker: The Visual Dictionary")* 66. [↑](#cite_ref-Fall_date_164-0) According to *[Star Wars Propaganda: A History of Persuasive Art in the Galaxy](/wiki/Star_Wars_Propaganda:_A_History_of_Persuasive_Art_in_the_Galaxy "Star Wars Propaganda: A History of Persuasive Art in the Galaxy")* the [Fall of the Old Republic](/wiki/Fall_of_the_Old_Republic "Fall of the Old Republic") took place prior to the founding of the [Galactic Republic](/wiki/Galactic_Republic "Galactic Republic"). *[The Star Wars Book](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_Book "The Star Wars Book")* states that the Galactic Republic was founded 1032 [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") before the events of [*Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope "Star Wars: Episode IV A New Hope"), which corrosponds to [1032 BBY](/wiki/1032_BBY "1032 BBY") per *[Star Wars: Galactic Atlas](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galactic_Atlas "Star Wars: Galactic Atlas")*. Therefore, the Fall of the Old Republic must have taken place prior to 1032 BBY 165. ↑ [165.0](#cite_ref-DB:Bane_165-0) [165.1](#cite_ref-DB:Bane_165-1) [165.2](#cite_ref-DB:Bane_165-2) [StarWars-DatabankII](/wiki/Databank_(2014-) "Databank (2014-)") [Darth Bane](https://www.starwars.com/databank/darth-bane) in the [Databank](/wiki/Databank_(2014-) "Databank (2014-)") ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20191016050833/https://www.starwars.com/databank/darth-bane)) 166.
